The Map Connector (also known as the Visual Editor) allows you to connect maps together.
The Map Connector (also known as the Visual Editor) allows you to connect maps together.
In the Debug menu (F9 or in the pause menu), choose the "Map Connections" option.
In the Debug menu (F9 or in the pause menu), choose the "Map Connections" option.
Once there, choose a map to display by pressing the S key. Select it and press the E key to edit its encounters, or double-click it to edit its metadata.
Once there, choose a map to display by pressing the S key.  Select it and press the E key to edit its encounters, or double-click it to edit its metadata.

Add additional maps to the canvas by pressing the A key, and drag them around to connect them.  Maps only connect if just their edges touch.
Every tile in a tileset has a terrain tag, which is a number. This number is used to give certain tiles special effects.
Every tile in a tileset has a terrain tag, which is a number.  This number is used to give certain tiles special effects.
For example, ledge tiles have terrain tag 1, which means the player jumps over them. Ledge tiles also have a single passable direction (set separately).
For example, ledge tiles have terrain tag 1, which means the player jumps over them.  Ledge tiles also have a single passable direction (set separately).
Grass tiles (in which you can have wild encounters) have terrain tag 2. Water tiles have terrain tag 6 or 7.
Grass tiles (in which you can have wild encounters) have terrain tag 2.  Water tiles have terrain tag 6 or 7.
Terrain tag 0 means the tile has no special effect. See the wiki for more information and a complete list of all terrain tags and their effects.
Terrain tag 0 means the tile has no special effect.  See the wiki for more information and a complete list of all terrain tags and their effects.
To set a tileset's terrain tags, open the Debug menu (F9 or from the pause menu) and choose "Edit Terrain Tags".
To set a tileset's terrain tags, open the Debug menu (F9 or from the pause menu) and choose "Edit Terrain Tags".

Every tile in a tileset has a terrain tag, which is a number. This number is used to give certain tiles special effects.
Every tile in a tileset has a terrain tag, which is a number.  This number is used to give certain tiles special effects.
For example, ledge tiles have terrain tag 1, which means the player jumps over them. Ledge tiles also have a single passable direction (set separately).
For example, ledge tiles have terrain tag 1, which means the player jumps over them.  Ledge tiles also have a single passable direction (set separately).
Grass tiles (in which you can have wild encounters) have terrain tag 2. Water tiles have terrain tag 6 or 7.
Grass tiles (in which you can have wild encounters) have terrain tag 2.  Water tiles have terrain tag 6 or 7.
Terrain tag 0 means the tile has no special effect. See the wiki for more information and a complete list of all terrain tags and their effects.
